The `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method in `/workspace/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` (lines 1405-1509) is trying to access `.target.model` on items in `self.select`.\n\n2. `self.select` is populated by the `get_select()` method, and each item in `self.select` is a tuple of `(expression, (sql, params), alias)`.\n\n3. The `expression` can be any type of expression - for model fields it's a `Col` object (which has a `.target` attribute), but for annotations it can be any expression type (like `Concat`, `Value`, `F`, etc.) which don't have a `.target` attribute.\n\n4. The code assumes all expressions have a `.target` attribute, causing an `AttributeError` when an annotation expression is encountered.\n\n5. The issue mentions that \"Prior to the `values()`/`values_list()` field ordering change, model field columns were always placed first in the SELECT clause.\" This means the code was written under the assumption that all `Col` objects would appear before any annotation expressions, so it would never encounter a non-Col expression when checking `.target.model`.\n\nLet me now find the fix. Bug Investigation\n\n## Files Examined\n- `/workspace/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` — Entry point `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method and related code\n- `/workspace/django/db/models/expressions.py` — Col and ColPairs expression classes\n- `/workspace/tests/select_for_update/tests.py` — Test cases for select_for_update functionality\n- `/workspace/tests/select_for_update/models.py` — Test models used in select_for_update tests\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: User-facing API call\n   - `Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")), \"born\")`\n   - Crash with `AttributeError` on `.target.model`\n\n2. **Called from**: Query execution path\n   - `SQLCompiler.as_sql()` or similar method that generates SQL\n   - Calls `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` at line 884 to get the OF arguments\n\n3. **Bug triggered by**: `/workspace/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py::get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` (line 1405)\n   - Specifically at lines 1424-1425 and line 1440\n   - These lines access `.target.model` on expressions in `self.select`\n   - But `self.select` can now contain annotation expressions (not just `Col` objects)\n   - Annotation expressions don't have a `.target` attribute\n\n4. **Root cause introduced by**: Commit `65ad4ade74dc9208b9d686a451cd6045df0c9c3a` (July 2024)\n   - Changed SELECT order to respect the order specified by `values()`/`values_list()`\n   - Before: order was always extra_fields + model_fields + annotations\n   - After: order respects user's specification, allowing annotations before model fields\n\n## Root Cause\n\n- **File**: `/workspace/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py`\n- **Function**: `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` (starting at line 1405)\n- **Problematic Lines**: \n  - Lines 1424-1425 (in `_get_parent_klass_info()` nested function)\n  - Line 1440 (in `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` nested function)\n- **Explanation**:\n\nThe `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method is responsible for generating the \"OF\" clause for SELECT FOR UPDATE queries. It iterates through `self.select` (which contains all selected expressions) and attempts to identify which model fields are being selected so it can lock the appropriate tables.\n\n**The Bug:**\nThe code assumes all items in `self.select[select_index][0]` are `Col` objects (which represent model field columns) and have a `.target` attribute. However, since commit `65ad4ade74dc9208b9d686a451cd6045df0c9c3a`, when `values()`/`values_list()` is called, the select list can contain annotation expressions (like `Concat`, `Value`, `F`, etc.) which may appear before model field columns. These annotation expressions do NOT have a `.target` attribute, causing an `AttributeError` when accessed.\n\n**Example of the issue:**\n```python\nPerson.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(\n    Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")),  # <- Annotation expression, no .target\n    \"born\"                              # <- Col object, has .target\n)\n```\n\nWhen the code tries to check if `self.select[0][0]` (the Concat expression) has `.target.model`, it crashes because `Concat` doesn't have a `.target` attribute.\n\n**Why the pattern `.target` is needed:**\n- The code needs to determine which model each selected column belongs to\n- Only `Col` objects (model field columns) have a `.target` attribute that points to the field\n- The `.target.model` tells the code which model owns that field\n- This is used to determine which table to lock in the SELECT FOR UPDATE OF clause\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nAdd a check to verify that the expression has a `.target` attribute before accessing it, similar to the pattern used elsewhere in the codebase (see line 213 in the same file).\n\n```diff\n        def _get_parent_klass_info(klass_info):\n            concrete_model = klass_info[\"model\"]._meta.concrete_model\n            for parent_model, parent_link in concrete_model._meta.parents.items():\n                all_parents = parent_model._meta.all_parents\n                yield {\n                    \"model\": parent_model,\n                    \"field\": parent_link,\n                    \"reverse\": False,\n                    \"select_fields\": [\n                        select_index\n-                       for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]\n+                       for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]\n                        # Selected columns from a model or its parents.\n-                       if (\n-                           self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model\n-                           or self.select[select_index][0].target.model in all_parents\n-                       )\n+                       if (\n+                           hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n+                           and (\n+                               self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model\n+                               or self.select[select_index][0].target.model in all_parents\n+                           )\n+                       )\n                    ],\n                }\n\n        def _get_first_selected_col_from_model(klass_info):\n            \"\"\"\n            Find the first selected column from a model. If it doesn't exist,\n            don't lock a model.\n\n            select_fields is filled recursively, so it also contains fields\n            from the parent models.\n            \"\"\"\n            concrete_model = klass_info[\"model\"]._meta.concrete_model\n            for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]:\n-               if self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model:\n+               if (\n+                   hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n+                   and self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model\n+               ):\n                    return self.select[select_index][0]\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Flow\n\n1. User calls: `Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(Concat(...), \"born\")`\n\n2. The ORM builds a Query object with:\n   - `select_for_update_of = (\"self\",)` — indicates which tables to lock\n   - `values_list([Concat(...), \"born\"])` — specifies which columns to select\n\n3. When generating SQL, the `SQLCompiler.as_sql()` method is called\n\n4. Inside `as_sql()`, at line 884, it calls:\n   ```python\n   of=self.get_select_for_update_of_arguments(),\n   ```\n\n5. This calls `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` which:\n   - Initializes `self.select` via `setup_query()` which calls `get_select()`\n   - `get_select()` builds `self.select` list with tuples of `(expression, (sql, params), alias)`\n   - The expressions can now be in any order (annotations first, then model fields)\n\n6. The method iterates through `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` indices to find model field columns\n\n7. For each index, it tries to check if the expression's model matches the target model:\n   - **Line 1424-1425** (Bug): `self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model`\n   - **Line 1440** (Bug): `self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model`\n\n8. If the expression at that index is an annotation (like `Concat`), accessing `.target` raises `AttributeError`\n\n### Why This is a Bug\n\nThe code was written under the assumption that model field columns (with `.target` attribute) always come before annotation expressions in the select list. This was true before commit `65ad4ade74dc9208b9d686a451cd6045df0c9c3a`, but now annotations can appear first.\n\nThe `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` indices point to positions in `self.select` where model field columns are located. However, because the code doesn't check if an expression has a `.target` attribute, it crashes when it encounters an annotation at a position where it expects a model field.\n\n### The Fix\n\nThe fix uses the same defensive pattern seen elsewhere in the codebase (line 213):\n```python\nhasattr(expr, \"target\") and expr.target.primary_key\n```\n\nBy wrapping the `.target` access with `hasattr()`, we:\n1. Skip annotation expressions that don't have `.target`\n2. Only process actual model field columns that have `.target`\n3. Correctly identify which tables need to be locked in the SELECT FOR UPDATE OF clause\n\nThe `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` list should only contain indices of model field columns, but the code must be defensive and handle the case where it encounters annotations due to the new field ordering feature.\nEOF\ncat /logs/agent/solution.md\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":0,"cache_creation_input_tokens":722,"cache_read_input_tokens":55195,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":722},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"d6159425-2464-4e9e-8d5a-bccfa6435922","uuid":"f080f69d-9f9b-4917-9598-96c37ded102f"}

And `cols` is either `self.get_default_columns()` or `self.query.select`.\n\nWhen `self.query.selected is not None`, the `klass_info` is created based on the ranges of default cols, but then the `selected` list is built from `self.query.selected`, which is the user-specified order.\n\nSo the issue is:\n1. `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` contains indices based on the assumption of the default order (extra_select + cols + annotations)\n2. Bug Investigation\n     2→\n     3→## Files Examined\n     4→- `/workspace/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` — Entry point `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method and related code\n     5→- `/workspace/django/db/models/expressions.py` — Col and ColPairs expression classes\n     6→- `/workspace/tests/select_for_update/tests.py` — Test cases for select_for_update functionality\n     7→- `/workspace/tests/select_for_update/models.py` — Test models used in select_for_update tests\n     8→\n     9→## Dependency Chain\n    10→\n    11→1. **Symptom observed in**: User-facing API call\n    12→   - `Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")), \"born\")`\n    13→   - Crash with `AttributeError` on `.target.model`\n    14→\n    15→2. **Called from**: Query execution path\n    16→   - Before: order was always extra_fields + model_fields + annotations\n    28→   - After: order respects user's specification, allowing annotations before model fields\n    29→\n    30→## Root Cause\n    31→\n    32→- **File**: `/workspace/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py`\n    33→- **Function**: `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` (starting at line 1405)\n    34→- **Problematic Lines**: \n    35→  - Lines 1424-1425 (in `_get_parent_klass_info()` nested function)\n    36→  - Line 1440 (in `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` nested function)\n    37→- **Explanation**:\n    38→\n    39→The `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method is responsible for generating the \"OF\" clause for SELECT FOR UPDATE queries. It iterates through `self.select` (which contains all selected expressions) and attempts to identify which model fields are being selected so it can lock the appropriate tables.\n    40→\n    41→**The Bug:**\n    42→The code assumes all items in `self.select[select_index][0]` are `Col` objects (which represent model field columns) and have a `.target` attribute. However, since commit `65ad4ade74dc9208b9d686a451cd6045df0c9c3a`, when `values()`/`values_list()` is called, the select list can contain annotation expressions (like `Concat`, `Value`, `F`, etc.) which may appear before model field columns. These annotation expressions do NOT have a `.target` attribute, causing an `AttributeError` when accessed.\n    43→\n    44→**Example of the issue:**\n    45→```python\n    46→Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(\n    47→    Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")),  # <- Annotation expression, no .target\n    48→    \"born\"                              # <- Col object, has .target\n    49→)\n    50→```\n    51→\n    52→When the code tries to check if `self.select[0][0]` (the Concat expression) has `.target.model`, it crashes because `Concat` doesn't have a `.target` attribute.\n    53→\n    54→**Why the pattern `.target` is needed:**\n    55→- The code needs to determine which model each selected column belongs to\n    56→- Only `Col` objects (model field columns) have a `.target` attribute that points to the field\n    57→- The `.target.model` tells the code which model owns that field\n    58→- This is used to determine which table to lock in the SELECT FOR UPDATE OF clause\n    59→\n    60→## Proposed Fix\n    61→\n    62→Add a check to verify that the expression has a `.target` attribute before accessing it, similar to the pattern used elsewhere in the codebase (see line 213 in the same file).\n    63→\n    64→```diff\n    65→        def _get_parent_klass_info(klass_info):\n    66→            concrete_model = klass_info[\"model\"]._meta.concrete_model\n    67→            for parent_model, parent_link in concrete_model._meta.parents.items():\n    68→                all_parents = parent_model._meta.all_parents\n    69→                yield {\n    70→                    \"model\": parent_model,\n    71→                    \"field\": parent_link,\n    72→                    \"reverse\": False,\n    73→                    \"select_fields\": [\n    74→                        select_index\n    75→-                       for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]\n    76→+                       for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]\n    77→                        # Selected columns from a model or its parents.\n    78→-                       if (\n    79→-                           self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model\n    80→-                           or self.select[select_index][0].target.model in all_parents\n    81→-                       )\n    82→+                       if (\n    83→+                           hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n    84→+                           and (\n    85→+                               self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model\n    86→+                               or self.select[select_index][0].target.model in all_parents\n    87→+                           )\n    88→+                       )\n    89→                    ],\n    90→                }\n    91→\n    92→        def _get_first_selected_col_from_model(klass_info):\n    93→            \"\"\"\n    94→            Find the first selected column from a model. If it doesn't exist,\n    95→            don't lock a model.\n    96→\n    97→            select_fields is filled recursively, so it also contains fields\n    98→            from the parent models.\n    99→            \"\"\"\n   100→            concrete_model = klass_info[\"model\"]._meta.concrete_model\n   101→            for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]:\n   102→-               if self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model:\n   103→+               if (\n   104→+                   hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n   105→+                   and self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model\n   106→+               ):\n   107→                    return self.select[select_index][0]\n   108→```\n   109→\n   110→## Analysis\n   111→\n   112→### Execution Flow\n   113→\n   114→1. User calls: `Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(Concat(...), \"born\")`\n   115→\n   116→2. The ORM builds a Query object with:\n   117→   - `select_for_update_of = (\"self\",)` — indicates which tables to lock\n   118→   - `values_list([Concat(...), \"born\"])` — specifies which columns to select\n   119→\n   120→3. When generating SQL, the `SQLCompiler.as_sql()` method is called\n   121→\n   122→4. Inside `as_sql()`, at line 884, it calls:\n   123→   ```python\n   124→   of=self.get_select_for_update_of_arguments(),\n   125→   ```\n   126→\n   127→5. This calls `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` which:\n   128→   - Initializes `self.select` via `setup_query()` which calls `get_select()`\n   129→   - `get_select()` builds `self.select` list with tuples of `(expression, (sql, params), alias)`\n   130→   - The expressions can now be in any order (annotations first, then model fields)\n   131→\n   132→6. The method iterates through `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` indices to find model field columns\n   133→\n   134→7. For each index, it tries to check if the expression's model matches the target model:\n   135→   - **Line 1424-1425** (Bug): `self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model`\n   136→   - **Line 1440** (Bug): `self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model`\n   137→\n   138→8. If the expression at that index is an annotation (like `Concat`), accessing `.target` raises `AttributeError`\n   139→\n   140→### Why This is a Bug\n   141→\n   142→The code was written under the assumption that model field columns (with `.target` attribute) always come before annotation expressions in the select list. This was true before commit `65ad4ade74dc9208b9d686a451cd6045df0c9c3a`, but now annotations can appear first.\n   143→\n   144→The `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` indices point to positions in `self.select` where model field columns are located. However, because the code doesn't check if an expression has a `.target` attribute, it crashes when it encounters an annotation at a position where it expects a model field.\n   145→\n   146→### The Fix\n   147→\n   148→The fix uses the same defensive pattern seen elsewhere in the codebase (line 213):\n   149→```python\n   150→hasattr(expr, \"target\") and expr.target.primary_key\n   151→```\n   152→\n   153→By wrapping the `.target` access with `hasattr()`, we:\n   154→1. Skip annotation expressions that don't have `.target`\n   155→2. Only process actual model field columns that have `.target`\n   156→3. Correctly identify which tables need to be locked in the SELECT FOR UPDATE OF clause\n   157→\n   158→The `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` list should only contain indices of model field columns, but the code must be defensive and handle the case where it encounters annotations due to the new field ordering feature.\n   159→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Specifically at lines 1424-1425 and line 1440\n   - These lines access `.target.model` on expressions in `self.select`\n   - But `self.select` can now contain annotation expressions (not just `Col` objects)\n   - Annotation expressions don't have a `.target` attribute\n\n4. **Root cause introduced by**: Commit `65ad4ade74dc9208b9d686a451cd6045df0c9c3a` (July 2024)\n   - Changed SELECT order to respect the order specified by `values()`/`values_list()`\n   - Before: order was always extra_fields + model_fields + annotations\n   - After: order respects user's specification, allowing annotations before model fields\n\n## Root Cause\n\n- **File**: `/workspace/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py`\n- **Function**: `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` (starting at line 1405)\n- **Problematic Lines**: \n  - Lines 1424-1425 (in `_get_parent_klass_info()` nested function)\n  - Line 1440 (in `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` nested function)\n- **Explanation**:\n\nThe `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method is responsible for generating the \"OF\" clause for SELECT FOR UPDATE queries. It iterates through `self.select` (which contains all selected expressions) and attempts to identify which model fields are being selected so it can lock the appropriate tables.\n\n**The Bug:**\nThe code assumes all items in `self.select[select_index][0]` are `Col` objects (which represent model field columns) and have a `.target` attribute. However, since commit `65ad4ade74dc9208b9d686a451cd6045df0c9c3a`, when `values()`/`values_list()` is called, the select list can contain annotation expressions (like `Concat`, `Value`, `F`, etc.) which may appear before model field columns. These annotation expressions do NOT have a `.target` attribute, causing an `AttributeError` when accessed.\n\n**Example of the issue:**\n```python\nPerson.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(\n    Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")),  # <- Annotation expression, no .target\n    \"born\"                              # <- Col object, has .target\n)\n```\n\nWhen the code tries to check if `self.select[0][0]` (the Concat expression) has `.target.model`, it crashes because `Concat` doesn't have a `.target` attribute.\n\n**Why the pattern `.target` is needed:**\n- The code needs to determine which model each selected column belongs to\n- Only `Col` objects (model field columns) have a `.target` attribute that points to the field\n- The `.target.model` tells the code which model owns that field\n- This is used to determine which table to lock in the SELECT FOR UPDATE OF clause\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nAdd a check to verify that the expression has a `.target` attribute before accessing it, similar to the pattern used elsewhere in the codebase (see line 213 in the same file).\n\n```diff\n        def _get_parent_klass_info(klass_info):\n            concrete_model = klass_info[\"model\"]._meta.concrete_model\n            for parent_model, parent_link in concrete_model._meta.parents.items():\n                all_parents = parent_model._meta.all_parents\n                yield {\n                    \"model\": parent_model,\n                    \"field\": parent_link,\n                    \"reverse\": False,\n                    \"select_fields\": [\n                        select_index\n-                       for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]\n+                       for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]\n                        # Selected columns from a model or its parents.\n-                       if (\n-                           self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model\n-                           or self.select[select_index][0].target.model in all_parents\n-                       )\n+                       if (\n+                           hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n+                           and (\n+                               self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model\n+                               or self.select[select_index][0].target.model in all_parents\n+                           )\n+                       )\n                    ],\n                }\n\n        def _get_first_selected_col_from_model(klass_info):\n            \"\"\"\n            Find the first selected column from a model. If it doesn't exist,\n            don't lock a model.\n\n            select_fields is filled recursively, so it also contains fields\n            from the parent models.\n            \"\"\"\n            concrete_model = klass_info[\"model\"]._meta.concrete_model\n            for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]:\n-               if self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model:\n+               if (\n+                   hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n+                   and self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model\n+               ):\n                    return self.select[select_index][0]\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Flow\n\n1. User calls: `Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(Concat(...), \"born\")`\n\n2. The ORM builds a Query object with:\n   - `select_for_update_of = (\"self\",)` — indicates which tables to lock\n   - `values_list([Concat(...), \"born\"])` — specifies which columns to select\n\n3. When generating SQL, the `SQLCompiler.as_sql()` method is called\n\n4. Inside `as_sql()`, at line 884, it calls:\n   ```python\n   of=self.get_select_for_update_of_arguments(),\n   ```\n\n5. This calls `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` which:\n   - Initializes `self.select` via `setup_query()` which calls `get_select()`\n   - `get_select()` builds `self.select` list with tuples of `(expression, (sql, params), alias)`\n   - The expressions can now be in any order (annotations first, then model fields)\n\n6. The method iterates through `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` indices to find model field columns\n\n7. For each index, it tries to check if the expression's model matches the target model:\n   - **Line 1424-1425** (Bug): `self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model`\n   - **Line 1440** (Bug): `self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model`\n\n8. If the expression at that index is an annotation (like `Concat`), accessing `.target` raises `AttributeError`\n\n### Why This is a Bug\n\nThe code was written under the assumption that model field columns (with `.target` attribute) always come before annotation expressions in the select list. This was true before commit `65ad4ade74dc9208b9d686a451cd6045df0c9c3a`, but now annotations can appear first.\n\nThe `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` indices point to positions in `self.select` where model field columns are located. However, because the code doesn't check if an expression has a `.target` attribute, it crashes when it encounters an annotation at a position where it expects a model field.\n\n### The Fix\n\nThe fix uses the same defensive pattern seen elsewhere in the codebase (line 213):\n```python\nhasattr(expr, \"target\") and expr.target.primary_key\n```\n\nBy wrapping the `.target` access with `hasattr()`, we:\n1. Skip annotation expressions that don't have `.target`\n2. Only process actual model field columns that have `.target`\n3. Correctly identify which tables need to be locked in the SELECT FOR UPDATE OF clause\n\nThe `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` list should only contain indices of model field columns, but the code must be defensive and handle the case where it encounters annotations due to the new field ordering feature.\n","numLines":159,"startLine":1,"totalLines":159}}}

It iterates through `self.select` (which contains all selected expressions) and attempts to identify which model fields are being selected so it can lock the appropriate tables.\n\n**The Bug:**\nThe code assumes all items in `self.select[select_index][0]` are `Col` objects (which represent model field columns) and have a `.target` attribute. <- Annotation expression, no .target\n    \"born\"                              # <- Col object, has .target\n)\n```\n\nWhen the code tries to check if `self.select[0][0]` (the Concat expression) has `.target.model`, it crashes because `Concat` doesn't have a `.target` attribute.\n\n**Why the pattern `.target` is needed:**\n- The code needs to determine which model each selected column belongs to\n- Only `Col` objects (model field columns) have a `.target` attribute that points to the field\n- The `.target.model` tells the code which model owns that field\n- This is used to determine which table to lock in the SELECT FOR UPDATE OF clause\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nAdd a check to verify that the expression has a `.target` attribute before accessing it, similar to the pattern used elsewhere in the codebase (see line 213 in the same file).\n\n```diff\n        def _get_parent_klass_info(klass_info):\n            concrete_model = klass_info[\"model\"]._meta.concrete_model\n            for parent_model, parent_link in concrete_model._meta.parents.items():\n                all_parents = parent_model._meta.all_parents\n                yield {\n                    \"model\": parent_model,\n                    \"field\": parent_link,\n                    \"reverse\": False,\n                    \"select_fields\": [\n                        select_index\n-                       for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]\n+                       for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]\n                        # If it doesn't exist,\n            don't lock a model.\n\n            select_fields is filled recursively, so it also contains fields\n            from the parent models.\n            \"\"\"\n            concrete_model = klass_info[\"model\"]._meta.concrete_model\n            for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]:\n-               if self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model:\n+               if (\n+                   hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n+                   and self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model\n+               ):\n                    return self.select[select_index][0]\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Flow\n\n1. Bug Investigation\n\n## Files Examined\n- `/workspace/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` — Entry point `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method and related code\n- `/workspace/django/db/models/expressions.py` — Col and ColPairs expression classes\n- `/workspace/tests/select_for_update/tests.py` — Test cases for select_for_update functionality\n- `/workspace/tests/select_for_update/models.py` — Test models used in select_for_update tests\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: User-facing API call\n   - `Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")), \"born\")`\n   - Crash with `AttributeError` on `.target.model`\n\n2. **Called from**: Query execution path\n   - `SQLCompiler.as_sql()` or similar method that generates SQL\n   - Calls `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` at line 884 to get the OF arguments\n\n3. **Bug triggered by**: `/workspace/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py::get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` (line 1405)\n   - Specifically at lines 1424-1425 and line 1440\n   - These lines access `.target.model` on expressions in `self.select`\n   - But `self.select` can now contain annotation expressions (not just `Col` objects)\n   - Annotation expressions don't have a `.target` attribute\n\n4. **Root cause introduced by**: Commit `65ad4ade74dc9208b9d686a451cd6045df0c9c3a` (July 2024)\n   - Changed SELECT order to respect the order specified by `values()`/`values_list()`\n   - Before: order was always extra_fields + model_fields + annotations\n   - After: order respects user's specification, allowing annotations before model fields\n\n## Root Cause\n\n- **File**: `/workspace/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py`\n- **Function**: `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` (starting at line 1405)\n- **Problematic Lines**: \n  - Lines 1424-1425 (in `_get_parent_klass_info()` nested function)\n  - Line 1440 (in `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` nested function)\n- **Explanation**:\n\nThe `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method is responsible for generating the \"OF\" clause for SELECT FOR UPDATE queries. It iterates through `self.select` (which contains all selected expressions) and attempts to identify which model fields are being selected so it can lock the appropriate tables.\n\n**The Bug:**\nThe code assumes all items in `self.select[select_index][0]` are `Col` objects (which represent model field columns) and have a `.target` attribute. However, since commit `65ad4ade74dc9208b9d686a451cd6045df0c9c3a`, when `values()`/`values_list()` is called, the select list can contain annotation expressions (like `Concat`, `Value`, `F`, etc.) which may appear before model field columns. These annotation expressions do NOT have a `.target` attribute, causing an `AttributeError` when accessed.\n\n**Example of the issue:**\n```python\nPerson.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(\n    Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")),  # <- Annotation expression, no .target\n    \"born\"                              # <- Col object, has .target\n)\n```\n\nWhen the code tries to check if `self.select[0][0]` (the Concat expression) has `.target.model`, it crashes because `Concat` doesn't have a `.target` attribute.\n\n**Why the pattern `.target` is needed:**\n- The code needs to determine which model each selected column belongs to\n- Only `Col` objects (model field columns) have a `.target` attribute that points to the field\n- The `.target.model` tells the code which model owns that field\n- This is used to determine which table to lock in the SELECT FOR UPDATE OF clause\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nAdd a check to verify that the expression has a `.target` attribute before accessing it, similar to the pattern used elsewhere in the codebase (see line 213 in the same file).\n\n```diff\n        def _get_parent_klass_info(klass_info):\n            concrete_model = klass_info[\"model\"]._meta.concrete_model\n            for parent_model, parent_link in concrete_model._meta.parents.items():\n                all_parents = parent_model._meta.all_parents\n                yield {\n                    \"model\": parent_model,\n                    \"field\": parent_link,\n                    \"reverse\": False,\n                    \"select_fields\": [\n                        select_index\n-                       for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]\n+                       for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]\n                        # Selected columns from a model or its parents.\n-                       if (\n-                           self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model\n-                           or self.select[select_index][0].target.model in all_parents\n-                       )\n+                       if (\n+                           hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n+                           and (\n+                               self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model\n+                               or self.select[select_index][0].target.model in all_parents\n+                           )\n+                       )\n                    ],\n                }\n\n        def _get_first_selected_col_from_model(klass_info):\n            \"\"\"\n            Find the first selected column from a model. If it doesn't exist,\n            don't lock a model.\n\n            select_fields is filled recursively, so it also contains fields\n            from the parent models.\n            \"\"\"\n            concrete_model = klass_info[\"model\"]._meta.concrete_model\n            for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]:\n-               if self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model:\n+               if (\n+                   hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n+                   and self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model\n+               ):\n                    return self.select[select_index][0]\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Flow\n\n1. User calls: `Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(Concat(...), \"born\")`\n\n2. The ORM builds a Query object with:\n   - `select_for_update_of = (\"self\",)` — indicates which tables to lock\n   - `values_list([Concat(...), \"born\"])` — specifies which columns to select\n\n3. When generating SQL, the `SQLCompiler.as_sql()` method is called\n\n4. Inside `as_sql()`, at line 884, it calls:\n   ```python\n   of=self.get_select_for_update_of_arguments(),\n   ```\n\n5. This calls `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` which:\n   - Initializes `self.select` via `setup_query()` which calls `get_select()`\n   - `get_select()` builds `self.select` list with tuples of `(expression, (sql, params), alias)`\n   - The expressions can now be in any order (annotations first, then model fields)\n\n6. The method iterates through `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` indices to find model field columns\n\n7. For each index, it tries to check if the expression's model matches the target model:\n   - **Line 1424-1425** (Bug): `self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model`\n   - **Line 1440** (Bug): `self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model`\n\n8. If the expression at that index is an annotation (like `Concat`), accessing `.target` raises `AttributeError`\n\n### Why This is a Bug\n\nThe root cause lies in the interaction between two parts of the code:\n\n1. **`klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` calculation** (lines 262-266 in `get_select()`):\n   - Created when `cols` is populated from either `get_default_columns()` or `self.query.select`\n   - The indices are calculated as `range(len(self.query.extra_select), len(self.query.extra_select) + len(cols))`\n   - These indices assume the order will be: extra_select + cols + annotations\n   - This was correct BEFORE commit `65ad4ade74dc9208b9d686a451cd6045df0c9c3a`\n\n2. **`self.query.selected` override** (lines 279-290 in `get_select()`):\n   - When `values()`/`values_list()` is called, `self.query.selected` is set with the user-specified order\n   - The `selected` list is built from `self.query.selected`, which can have annotations BEFORE model fields\n   - This new order is stored in `ret` (which becomes `self.select`)\n   - This was introduced BY commit `65ad4ade74dc9208b9d686a451cd6045df0c9c3a`\n\n3. **The mismatch**:\n   - `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` still contains indices based on the OLD order assumption (extra_select + cols + annotations)\n   - But `self.select` now contains expressions in the NEW order (user-specified from `values()`/`values_list()`)\n   - When `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` tries to use those indices to access columns, they may point to annotation expressions instead of Col objects\n\n4. **The crash**:\n   - The code at lines 1424-1425 and 1440 tries to access `.target.model` on the expression at each index\n   - If that index points to an annotation expression (not a Col object), accessing `.target` raises `AttributeError`\n   - Example: If the user specifies `values_list(Concat(...), \"born\")`, the Concat annotation is at index 0, but `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` might incorrectly reference index 0 expecting a Col object\n\nThe code was written under the assumption that model field columns (with `.target` attribute) always come before annotation expressions in the select list. This was true before commit `65ad4ade74dc9208b9d686a451cd6045df0c9c3a`, but now annotations can appear first.\n\n### The Fix\n\nThe fix uses the same defensive pattern seen elsewhere in the codebase (line 213):\n```python\nhasattr(expr, \"target\") and expr.target.primary_key\n```\n\nBy wrapping the `.target` access with `hasattr()`, we:\n1. Skip annotation expressions that don't have `.target`\n2. Only process actual model field columns that have `.target`\n3. Correctly identify which tables need to be locked in the SELECT FOR UPDATE OF clause\n\nThe `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` list should only contain indices of model field columns, but the code must be defensive and handle the case where it encounters annotations due to the new field ordering feature.\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":109,"oldLines":34,"newStart":109,"newLines":42,"lines":[" "," ## Analysis"," ","-### Execution Flow","+### Detailed Execution Flow"," ","-1. Bug Investigation\n     2→\n     3→## Files Examined\n     4→- `/workspace/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` — Entry point `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method and related code\n     5→- `/workspace/django/db/models/expressions.py` — Col and ColPairs expression classes\n     6→- `/workspace/tests/select_for_update/tests.py` — Test cases for select_for_update functionality\n     7→- `/workspace/tests/select_for_update/models.py` — Test models used in select_for_update tests\n     8→\n     9→## Dependency Chain\n    10→\n    11→1. **Symptom observed in**: User-facing API call\n    12→   - Before: order was always extra_fields + model_fields + annotations\n    28→   - After: order respects user's specification, allowing annotations before model fields\n    29→\n    30→## Root Cause\n    31→\n    32→- **File**: `/workspace/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py`\n    33→- **Function**: `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` (starting at line 1405)\n    34→- **Problematic Lines**: \n    35→  - Lines 1424-1425 (in `_get_parent_klass_info()` nested function)\n    36→  - Line 1440 (in `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` nested function)\n    37→- **Explanation**:\n    38→\n    39→The `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method is responsible for generating the \"OF\" clause for SELECT FOR UPDATE queries. It iterates through `self.select` (which contains all selected expressions) and attempts to identify which model fields are being selected so it can lock the appropriate tables.\n    40→\n    41→**The Bug:**\n    42→The code assumes all items in `self.select[select_index][0]` are `Col` objects (which represent model field columns) and have a `.target` attribute. However, since commit `65ad4ade74dc9208b9d686a451cd6045df0c9c3a`, when `values()`/`values_list()` is called, the select list can contain annotation expressions (like `Concat`, `Value`, `F`, etc.) which may appear before model field columns. These annotation expressions do NOT have a `.target` attribute, causing an `AttributeError` when accessed.\n    43→\n    44→**Example of the issue:**\n    45→```python\n    46→Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(\n    47→    Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")),  # <- Annotation expression, no .target\n    48→    \"born\"                              # <- Col object, has .target\n    49→)\n    50→```\n    51→\n    52→When the code tries to check if `self.select[0][0]` (the Concat expression) has `.target.model`, it crashes because `Concat` doesn't have a `.target` attribute.\n    53→\n    54→**Why the pattern `.target` is needed:**\n    55→- The code needs to determine which model each selected column belongs to\n    56→- Only `Col` objects (model field columns) have a `.target` attribute that points to the field\n    57→- The `.target.model` tells the code which model owns that field\n    58→- This is used to determine which table to lock in the SELECT FOR UPDATE OF clause\n    59→\n    60→## Proposed Fix\n    61→\n    62→Add a check to verify that the expression has a `.target` attribute before accessing it, similar to the pattern used elsewhere in the codebase (see line 213 in the same file).\n    63→\n    64→```diff\n    65→        def _get_parent_klass_info(klass_info):\n    66→            concrete_model = klass_info[\"model\"]._meta.concrete_model\n    67→            for parent_model, parent_link in concrete_model._meta.parents.items():\n    68→                all_parents = parent_model._meta.all_parents\n    69→                yield {\n    70→                    \"model\": parent_model,\n    71→                    \"field\": parent_link,\n    72→                    \"reverse\": False,\n    73→                    \"select_fields\": [\n    74→                        select_index\n    75→-                       for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]\n    76→+                       for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]\n    77→                        # Creates `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` based on the range of model field columns\n   135→     - But this range assumes the OLD order, not the user-specified order\n   136→\n   137→5. **The mismatch becomes clear**:\n   138→   - `self.select` now has: `[(Concat(...), sql, alias), (\"born\" Col, sql, alias), ...]`\n   139→   - `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` contains indices like `[0, 1]` expecting Col objects\n   140→   - But index 0 points to a Concat expression, not a Col\n   141→\n   142→6. **The crash** (lines 1424-1425 and 1440):\n   143→   - Code tries: `self.select[0][0].target.model`\n   144→   - `self.select[0][0]` is the Concat expression\n   145→   - Concat doesn't have a `.target` attribute\n   146→   - Result: `AttributeError: 'Concat' object has no attribute 'target'`\n   147→\n   148→### Why This is a Bug\n   149→\n   150→The root cause lies in the interaction between two parts of the code:\n   151→\n   152→1. **`klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` calculation** (lines 262-266 in `get_select()`):\n   153→   - Created when `cols` is populated from either `get_default_columns()` or `self.query.select`\n   154→   - The indices are calculated as `range(len(self.query.extra_select), len(self.query.extra_select) + len(cols))`\n   155→   - These indices assume the order will be: extra_select + cols + annotations\n   156→   - This was correct BEFORE commit `65ad4ade74dc9208b9d686a451cd6045df0c9c3a`\n   157→\n   158→2. **`self.query.selected` override** (lines 279-290 in `get_select()`):\n   159→   - When `values()`/`values_list()` is called, `self.query.selected` is set with the user-specified order\n   160→   - The `selected` list is built from `self.query.selected`, which can have annotations BEFORE model fields\n   161→   - This new order is stored in `ret` (which becomes `self.select`)\n   162→   - This was introduced BY commit `65ad4ade74dc9208b9d686a451cd6045df0c9c3a`\n   163→\n   164→3. **The mismatch**:\n   165→   - `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` still contains indices based on the OLD order assumption (extra_select + cols + annotations)\n   166→   - But `self.select` now contains expressions in the NEW order (user-specified from `values()`/`values_list()`)\n   167→   - When `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` tries to use those indices to access columns, they may point to annotation expressions instead of Col objects\n   168→\n   169→4. **The crash**:\n   170→   - The code at lines 1424-1425 and 1440 tries to access `.target.model` on the expression at each index\n   171→   - If that index points to an annotation expression (not a Col object), accessing `.target` raises `AttributeError`\n   172→   - Example: If the user specifies `values_list(Concat(...), \"born\")`, the Concat annotation is at index 0, but `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` might incorrectly reference index 0 expecting a Col object\n   173→\n   174→The code was written under the assumption that model field columns (with `.target` attribute) always come before annotation expressions in the select list. This was true before commit `65ad4ade74dc9208b9d686a451cd6045df0c9c3a`, but now annotations can appear first.\n   175→\n   176→### The Fix\n   177→\n   178→The fix uses the same defensive pattern seen elsewhere in the codebase (line 213):\n   179→```python\n   180→hasattr(expr, \"target\") and expr.target.primary_key\n   181→```\n   182→\n   183→By wrapping the `.target` access with `hasattr()`, we:\n   184→1. Skip annotation expressions that don't have `.target`\n   185→2. Only process actual model field columns that have `.target`\n   186→3. Correctly identify which tables need to be locked in the SELECT FOR UPDATE OF clause\n   187→\n   188→The `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` list should only contain indices of model field columns, but the code must be defensive and handle the case where it encounters annotations due to the new field ordering feature.\n   189→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. This new order is stored in `ret` (which becomes `self.select`)\n   - This was introduced BY commit `65ad4ade74dc9208b9d686a451cd6045df0c9c3a`\n\n3. **The mismatch**:\n   - `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` still contains indices based on the OLD order assumption (extra_select + cols + annotations)\n   - But `self.select` now contains expressions in the NEW order (user-specified from `values()`/`values_list()`)\n   - When `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` tries to use those indices to access columns, they may point to annotation expressions instead of Col objects\n\n4. **The crash**:\n   - The code at lines 1424-1425 and 1440 tries to access `.target.model` on the expression at each index\n   - If that index points to an annotation expression (not a Col object), accessing `.target` raises `AttributeError`\n   - Example: If the user specifies `values_list(Concat(...), \"born\")`, the Concat annotation is at index 0, but `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` might incorrectly reference index 0 expecting a Col object\n\nThe code was written under the assumption that model field columns (with `.target` attribute) always come before annotation expressions in the select list. This was true before commit `65ad4ade74dc9208b9d686a451cd6045df0c9c3a`, but now annotations can appear first.\n\n### The Fix\n\nThe fix uses the same defensive pattern seen elsewhere in the codebase (line 213):\n```python\nhasattr(expr, \"target\") and expr.target.primary_key\n```\n\nBy wrapping the `.target` access with `hasattr()`, we:\n1. Skip annotation expressions that don't have `.target`\n2. Only process actual model field columns that have `.target`\n3. Correctly identify which tables need to be locked in the SELECT FOR UPDATE OF clause\n\nThe `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` list should only contain indices of model field columns, but the code must be defensive and handle the case where it encounters annotations due to the new field ordering feature.\n","numLines":189,"startLine":1,"totalLines":189}}}
